--- Commit Message ---
LU-18357 ptlrpc: Use nodemap IAM for persisting filesets

Currently, two separate commands exist to set a fileset and both
behave differently. "lctl set_param (-P)" works as expected. On the
other hand, "lctl nodemap_set_fileset" updates the fileset only on the
local node and is not persistent. It could also be run from other
server nodes and not only from the MGS. This behavior is inconsistent
with other nodemap commands.

Ideally, we would want to use the nodemap IAM records for persisting
all nodemap properties without relying on secondary mechanisms, such
as the params llog which is currently used for filesets. This patch
adds support for persistence across restarts for "lctl
nodemap_set_fileset" commands. Filesets are split into 28 byte path
fragments which are stored alongside 4 byte fragment metadata into one
nodemap IAM record (which is 32 bytes).

For this, fileset fragments are stored in a "defined" subid range
within the NODEMAP_CLUSTER_IDX type. In anticipation of supporting
multiple filesets, the first fileset subid is reserved for a fileset
header. The subid range is set to support at maximum 256 nodemap
records for fileset fragments.  256 entries support enough fragments
to hold a PATH_MAX fileset in total. Only needed fragments are
inserted into the nodemap IAM.

To support seamless updates from fileset llog to IAM versions, a
nodemap flag was added which allows existing "lctl set_param -P
nodemap.<name>.fileset" to be applied outside the nodemap IAM as long
as no IAM records were set. Filesets from the llog are not migrated to
the IAM but are still compatbiel after an update. "lctl set_param
nodemap.<name>.fileset" is deprecated and uses the IAM once fileset
IAM records are in use.

Sanity-sec "test_27a" was modified to test fileset persistence.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-10-22 20:49:35.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2: Code-Review-1

(9 comments)

I was thinking this would just run the equivalent of "lctl set_param -P ...=fileset" in jt_nodemap_set_fileset() when "lctl nodemap_set_fileset" was run on the MGS, since it always needs to be run on the MGS anyway.

Is the extra kernel complexity worthwhile/necessary, or would this patch be simplified by handling this in userspace?  Is there a downside to handling this in userspace?

Passed enforced test review-dne-part-3 on RHEL 9.3 / x86_64 uploaded by Onyx Autotest 2 from onyx-147vm1: https://testing.whamcloud.com/test_sessions/a296091b-5d48-4b18-894e-c85f47067506 ran 3 tests.

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-10-23 12:03:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

(7 comments)

> Patch Set 2: Code-Review-1
> 
> (9 comments)
> 
> I was thinking this would just run the equivalent of "lctl set_param -P ...=fileset" in jt_nodemap_set_fileset() when "lctl nodemap_set_fileset" was run on the MGS, since it always needs to be run on the MGS anyway.
> 
> Is the extra kernel complexity worthwhile/necessary, or would this patch be simplified by handling this in userspace?  Is there a downside to handling this in userspace?

Andreas, thank you for the quick review!

I was considering this at first, and it would be enough in the way filesets are handled on "master" because only "set" and "get" exist, so "lctl nodemap_set_fileset" can simply be rerouted in user space. 

It becomes more complex when supporting multiple filesets per nodemap with new commands like "lctl nodemap_{add,del}_fileset" or potentially others in the future. To use the "params" llog, we have "lctl set_param -P" available, but we cannot change how it behaves in order to be consistent with the landed version. It must therefore overwrite the existing fileset. This means that "lctl set_param" must also support multiple filesets (even if only internally). 

Consider the following future situation:
- "lctl nodemap_add_fileset --name <nm_name> --fileset /foo"
- "lctl nodemap_add_fileset --name <nm_name> --fileset /bar"

This would extend to something like this with a new separator ":" (not supported in this patch) so that each entry in the llog is a snapshot of all filesets per nodemap:
- "lctl set_param nodemap.<nm_name>.fileset='/foo:/bar'" (llog entry)

In this case, redirecting the "add" call in user space no longer works because you need all filesets to persist them. So, instead of issuing three calls from user space: add one new fileset, get all filesets, "set_param -P" with all filesets, this patch does it directly on the MGS-side. 

I don't think we gain much doing it in user space except that we don't need to forge an "lcfg" anymore, but instead, we would need more complexity to communicate through ioctl. In any case, separating nodemap and fileset commands seems to be necessary.

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-11-05 19:36:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

(12 comments)

> Patch Set 4: Code-Review-1
> 
> (12 comments)
> 
> I am wondering if this is going to break fileset handling in case of upgrade of an existing file system that already has nodemaps with fileset. Have you tried this? You could format a new file system without this patch, define nodemaps with fileset, and then upgrade the code with this patch, and see if your fileset is still there, on MGS and MDS and OSS servers.

Sebastien, thank you for the review.

Yes, I have tried this case, and it is not breaking fileset handling when upgrading (or even downgrading). It remains compatible because the params llog format for setting a fileset is unchanged and the forged lustre_cfg is equivalent to what "lctl set_param -P nodemap.<nm>.fileset=..." would generate. 

Note that with or without this patch, the MGS does not load the fileset on restart because the params llog is not loaded (which still needs to be dealt with in another patch). It does not affect the functionality of the fileset in any case because the MDS is the important one when a client connects to get the FS root path.

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2024-11-06 09:38:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

Nice, the 'lctl nodemap_set_fileset' now setting the parameter permanently is very useful!

I am wondering if we could go one step further with this patch and prevent the use of 'lctl set_param nodemap.xx.fileset' on all nodes? (We cannot do anything for -P, as it just insert the provided string in the params llog, for it to be processed later) For instance, other nodemap properties cannot be set with set_param:

   # lctl set_param nodemap.nm0.squash_uid=99
   error: set_param: setting 'nodemap/nm0/squash_uid'='99': Input/output error

So it should be the same for the fileset, and return an error if this method is used instead of 'lctl nodemap_set_fileset' (possibly with a message indicating the right way to proceed).

Patch Set 5:

Passed enforced test review-dne-part-2 on RHEL 9.3 / x86_64 uploaded by Onyx Autotest 2 from onyx-153vm1: https://testing.whamcloud.com/test_sessions/11f7c6d4-dfa9-4d60-ade8-86d9e3aeff96 ran 7 tests.

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-11-06 21:26:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

(3 comments)

> Patch Set 5:
> 
> Nice, the 'lctl nodemap_set_fileset' now setting the parameter permanently is very useful!
> 
> I am wondering if we could go one step further with this patch and prevent the use of 'lctl set_param nodemap.xx.fileset' on all nodes? (We cannot do anything for -P, as it just insert the provided string in the params llog, for it to be processed later) For instance, other nodemap properties cannot be set with set_param:
> 
>    # lctl set_param nodemap.nm0.squash_uid=99
>    error: set_param: setting 'nodemap/nm0/squash_uid'='99': Input/output error
> 
> So it should be the same for the fileset, and return an error if this method is used instead of 'lctl nodemap_set_fileset' (possibly with a message indicating the right way to proceed).

I don't think we can easily do it in this case. The challenge is that we cannot differentiate right now whether "lctl set_param nodemap.xx.fileset" was issued by an "lctl" of a user, by lctl set_param -P" from on another node, or by the params llog. Ultimately, what the "-P" argument does here, on a high-level, is calling on other server nodes, record that action as an lctl command to the params llog, and then upcall it as an lctl command, which just writes this action into a proc file (which you could also do manually). This upcall also occurs when the llog is read.

"lctl nodemap_*" commands operate through ioctl, and blocking "lctl set_param" for them is straightforward. In the specific case of "nodemap.nm0.squash_uid", no "seq_write" function is defined, and therefore, writing to the proc file with that action is invalid -> EIO.  

Something similar could be done for the "nodemap.xx.fileset" action, but we would need a new action for filesets then to persist them in the llog. This would also break backward compatibility because of the new name. Overall, this is really messy and I don't think we should consider it.

If there are no other ideas, I think we should pursue this in another patch if needed because it may require more extensive changes.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-11-06 22:37:26.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5: Code-Review-1

> I am wondering if we could go one step further with this patch and
 > prevent the use of 'lctl set_param nodemap.xx.fileset' on all nodes?

I don't think this is very urgent.

The "fileset" property is only used on the MDTs (so not exposed to clients to mess with).

I agree with Marc that it is difficult/impossible to distinguish between "lctl nodemap_set_fileset" and "lctl set_param" and "lctl set_param -P", especially since "-P" just (indirectly) results in "lctl set_param" being called on all the nodes via a UDEV upcall.

 > Failed enforced test review-dne-selinux-ssk-part-2 on RHEL 8.9 /
 > x86_64 uploaded by Trevis Autotest 2 from trevis-66vm1:
 > https://testing.whamcloud.com/test_sessions/de9b8b09-3674-4318-8e7f-3dcdac89716c
 > ran 5 tests.  1 tests failed: sanity-sec.

It looks like sanity-sec test_30b has failed 3x with this patch in the past 4 weeks, but no other patch, so it is likely to be a regression introduced by this change:

Patch Set 5:

(2 comments)

Thank you, Andreas. I have noticed it as well, although the reason was a bit obscured.

Patchset 5 should fix the regression in test "30b" introduced by the sanity-sec changes. Fileset testing is done on a single client. Previously, only this client was restarted. Because now everything is restarted, not all clients were mounted which caused 30b to fail. 

This further only affected tests where "SHARED_KEYs" are used (e.g., 30b) because they rely on an existing setup. 

All remaining clients are now remounted at the end of the fileset test. I'm not very familiar with SSK, though. @Sebastien, can you please check that I didn't miss any environment variables or similar for the SSK case and that the client mounting is correct?

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-12-11 15:31:43.000000000) ---
Patch Set 13:

(2 comments)

Thank you, Andreas and Yingjin, for your initial comments! 

Since all tests were passed, this patch is now ready for review. 

Two remarks:

First, regarding the usage of llog filesets as it might not be obvious. In this patch, llog filesets are not migrated to IAM (might not fit into IAM) and are never deleted from the llog. So, when the IAM is used for filesets (decided by the new nodemap flag), the llog entry is still loaded but no longer applied to the nodemap. 

It could be possible to upcall an "lctl set_param -d" on the nodemap fileset property as soon as the "use IAM" flag is set since it is no longer needed in the future. Nevertheless, the llog entry might still be needed in case of a downgrade, which is why it is kept in this patch. (we may want to delete the llog fileset entry when a nodemap is deleted though?)

Second, for the subsequent multi fileset patch, a global fileset id will be used in the fileset fragment nodemap IAM record. This is then used to offset the subid range. In addition, a subid range is reserved for a fileset header (not needed in this patch), e.g., for the read-only flag. This means we will have 1 primary fileset and 511 alternate fileset headers and filesets available.

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-12-12 16:58:18.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

(6 comments)

Patchset 14 changes the following, among others:
- Use 64 subids and allow filesets on the IAM up to 1791 + 1 characters.
- Revert the fileset size to 4096 + 1 for the in-memory nodemap struct. Larger than 1791 char filesets are only relevant when they come from the llog. They are further never migrated to the IAM so this is not an issue.
- Fix a bug when inserting the last fragment of a fileset, which fits a nodemap record fully.

--- Message (Marc Vef, 2024-12-13 16:10:25.000000000) ---
Patch Set 15:

(7 comments)

Andreas, thanks for the comments. This patch addresses those, in particular:
- Using 256 subids for filesets so that PATH_MAX fileset's can be stored. We can easily tune that down/up until it is landed.
- The patch still doesn't migrate llog filesets to the IAM. Although with 256 subids this would work, it has some unexpected side-effects, e.g., "lctl set_param nodemap.<nm>.fileset" would become persistent, because we can't distinguish whether we are called from "lctl set_param -P" or without "-P".
